//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/40px-Padlock-silver.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>\n     </a>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Effects of global warming\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       This article is primarily about effects during the 21st century. For longer-term effects, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Long-term_effects_of_global_warming" title="Long-term effects of global warming">\n        Long-term effects of global warming\n       </a>\n       . See also\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming_on_humans" title="Effects of global warming on humans">\n        Effects of global warming on humans\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg">\n         <img alt="Refer to caption and image description" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="992" data-file-width="939" height="423" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg/400px-Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg/600px-Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg/800px-Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg.png 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Impacts_of_global_warming_2_svg.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Summary of climate change impacts.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png">\n         <img alt="Refer to caption and image description" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png/400px-Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png/600px-Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png/800px-Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Projected global warming in 2100 for a range of emission scenarios.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        effects of\n        <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n         global warming\n        </a>\n       </b>\n       are the environmental and social changes caused (directly or indirectly) by human emissions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gases\n       </a>\n       . There is\n       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change" title="Scientific opinion on climate change">\n        a scientific consensus that climate change is occurring\n       </a>\n       , and that human activities are the primary driver.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many impacts of climate change have already been observed, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">\n        glacier retreat\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cramer_observed_effects_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cramer_observed_effects-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       changes in the timing of seasonal events\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cramer_observed_effects_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cramer_observed_effects-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (e.g., earlier flowering of plants),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and changes in agricultural productivity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cramer_observed_effects_2-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cramer_observed_effects-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Future effects of climate change will vary depending on\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_global_warming" title="Politics of global warming">\n        climate change policies\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adaptation_and_mitigation_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-adaptation_and_mitigation-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_development" title="Social development">\n        social development\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The two main policies to address climate change are reducing human greenhouse gas emissions (\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">\n        climate change mitigation\n       </a>\n       ) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_adaptation" title="Climate change adaptation">\n        adapting to the impacts\n       </a>\n       of climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_change_policy_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-climate_change_policy-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_engineering" title="Climate engineering">\n        Geoengineering\n       </a>\n       is another policy option.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_change_policy_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-climate_change_policy-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Near-term climate change policies could significantly affect long-term climate change impacts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adaptation_and_mitigation_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-adaptation_and_mitigation-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Stringent mitigation policies might be able to limit global warming (in 2100) to around 2\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C2%B0C" title="\xc2\xb0C">\n        \xc2\xb0C\n       </a>\n       or below, relative to pre-industrial levels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Without mitigation, increased\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_demand" title="Energy demand">\n        energy demand\n       </a>\n       and extensive use of\n       <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">\n        fossil fuels\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       might lead to global warming of around 4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Higher magnitudes of global warming would be more difficult to adapt to,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and would increase the risk of negative impacts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 Observed impacts\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-28">\n             <a href="#Projected_impacts_2">\n              <span         </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#Biological_systems">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Biological systems\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30">\n           <a href="#Observed_impacts_on_biological_systems">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Observed impacts on biological systems\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31">\n           <a href="#Projected_impacts_on_biological_systems">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Projected impacts on biological systems\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32">\n         <a href="#Abrupt_or_irreversible_changes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Abrupt or irreversible changes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33">\n           <a href="#Biogeochemical_cycles">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Biogeochemical cycles\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34">\n           <a href="#Greenland_and_West_Antarctic_Ice_sheets">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Greenland and West Antarctic Ice sheets\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35">\n           <a href="#Atlantic_Meridional_Overturning_Circulation">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Atlantic Meridional Overturning Circulation\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36">\n           <a href="#Irreversibilities">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Irreversibilities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-37">\n             <a href="#Commitment_to_radiative_forcing">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               7.4.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Commitment to radiative forcing\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-38">\n             <a href="#Irreversible_impacts">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               7.4.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Irreversible impacts\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39">\n         <a href="#Benefits_of_global_warming">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Benefits of global warming\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40">\n           <a href="#CO2_fertilisation_effect">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             CO2 fertilisation effect\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41">\n           <a href="#Human_health">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Human health\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42">\n           <a href="#Ice-free_Northwest_Passage">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Ice-free Northwest Passage\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43">\n           <a href="#Animal_population_changes">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Animal population changes\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44">\n         <a href="#Scientific_opinion">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Scientific opinion\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-45">\n           <a href="#NASA_data_and_tools">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             NASA data and tools\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47">\n         <a href="#Footnotes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Footnotes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">\n        Definitions\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Attribution_of_recent_climate_change" title="Attribution of recent climate change">\n        attribution of recent climate change\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In this article, "\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">\n        climate change\n       </a>\n       " means a change in climate that persists over a sustained period of time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">\n        World Meteorological Organization\n       </a>\n       defines this time period as 30 years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Examples of climate change include increases in global surface temperature (global warming), changes in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainfall" title="Rainfall">\n        rainfall\n       </a>\n       patterns, and changes in the frequency of\n       <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">\n        extreme weather\n       </a>\n       events. Changes in climate may be due to natural causes, e.g., changes in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">\n        sun\n       </a>\n       \'s output, or due to human activities, e.g., changing the composition of the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albritton_climate_change_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-albritton_climate_change-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Any human-induced changes in climate will occur against a background of natural climatic variations\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albritton_climate_change_16-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-albritton_climate_change-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and of variations in human activity such as population growth on shores or in arid areas which increase or decrease climate vulnerability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatureTaboo_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NatureTaboo-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Also, the term "anthropogenic forcing" refers to the influence exerted on a habitat or chemical environment by humans, as opposed to a natural process.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Temperature_changes">\n        Temperature changes\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg">\n           <img alt="Global mean surface temperature change since 1880, relative to the 1951\xe2\x80\x931980 mean, showing a long term warming trend." data-file-height="805" data-file-width="951" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/300px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/450px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/600px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Global mean surface temperature change since 1880, relative to the 1951\xe2\x80\x931980 mean. Source:\n          <a class="external text" href="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/" rel="nofollow">\n           NASA GISS\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_(2007).png">\n           <img alt="Refer to caption" data-file-height="338" data-file-width="728" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png/300px-Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png/450px-Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png/600px-Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png 2x" width="300"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          The graph above shows the average of a set of temperature simulations for the 20th century (black line), followed by projected temperatures for the 21st century based on three greenhouse gas emissions scenarios (colored lines).\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-herring_temperature_projections_19-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-herring_temperature_projections-19">\n            [19]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       This article breaks down some of the impacts of climate change according to different levels of future global warming. This way of describing impacts has, for instance, been used in the IPCC (\n       <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">\n        Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change\n       </a>\n       ) Assessment Reports on climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-table_of_key_vulnerabilities_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-table_of_key_vulnerabilities-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The instrumental\n       <a href="/wiki/Temperature_record" title="Temperature record">\n        temperature record\n       </a>\n       shows global warming of around 0.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C during the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="SRES_emissions_scenarios">\n        SRES emissions scenarios\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The future level of global warming is uncertain, but a wide range of estimates (projections) have been made.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The IPCC\'s "\n       <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">\n        SRES\n       </a>\n       " scenarios have been frequently used to make\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_climate_model#Projections_of_future_climate_change" title="Global climate model">\n        projections of future climate change\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :22\xe2\x80\x9324\n       </sup>\n       The SRES scenarios are "\n       <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_climate_change_mitigation#Baselines" title="Economics of climate change mitigation">\n        baseline\n       </a>\n       " (or "reference") scenarios, which means that they do not take into account any current or future measures to limit GHG emissions (e.g., the UNFCCC\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">\n        Kyoto Protocol\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2010 United Nations Climate Change Conference">\n        Canc\xc3\xban agreements\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Emissions projections of the SRES scenarios are broadly comparable in range to the baseline emissions scenarios that have been developed by the scientific community.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios_22-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">\n        IPCC Fourth Assessment Report\n       </a>\n       , changes in future global mean temperature were projected using the six SRES "marker" emissions scenarios.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Emissions projections for the six SRES "marker" scenarios are representative of the full set of forty SRES scenarios.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For the lowest emissions SRES marker scenario ("B1" \xe2\x80\x93 see the\n       <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">\n        SRES\n       </a>\n       article for details on this scenario), the best estimate for global mean temperature is an increase of 1.8\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (3.2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       by the end of the 21st century. This projection is relative to global temperatures at the end of the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The "likely" range (greater than 66% probability, based on expert judgement)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       for the SRES B1 marker scenario is 1.1\xe2\x80\x932.9\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (2.0\xe2\x80\x935.2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For the highest emissions SRES marker scenario (A1FI), the best estimate for global mean temperature increase is 4.0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (7.2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F), with a "likely" range of 2.4\xe2\x80\x936.4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (4.3\xe2\x80\x9311.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The range in temperature projections partly reflects (1) the choice of\n       <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_global_warming#Emissions_scenarios" title="Economics of global warming">\n        emissions scenario\n       </a>\n       , and (2) the "\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_sensitivity" title="Climate sensitivity">\n        climate sensitivity\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :22\xe2\x80\x9324\n       </sup>\n       For (1), different scenarios make different assumptions of future social and economic development (e.g.,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">\n        economic growth\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Population_projection" title="Population projection">\n        population level\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy" title="Energy policy">\n        energy policies\n       </a>\n       ), which in turn affects projections of greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :22\xe2\x80\x9324\n       </sup>\n       The projected magnitude of warming by 2100 is closely related to the level of cumulative emissions over the 21st century (i.e. total emissions between 2000\xe2\x80\x932100).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unep_cumulative_emissions_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-unep_cumulative_emissions-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The higher the cumulative emissions over this time period, the greater the level of warming is projected to occur.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unep_cumulative_emissions_30-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-unep_cumulative_emissions-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       (2) reflects uncertainty in the response of the climate system to past and future GHG emissions, which is measured by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_sensitivity" title="Climate sensitivity">\n        climate sensitivity\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :22\xe2\x80\x9324\n       </sup>\n       Higher estimates of climate sensitivity lead to greater projected warming, while lower estimates of climate sensitivity lead to less projected warming.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Over the next several millennia, projections suggest that global warming could be irreversible.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_irreversible_climate_change_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-solomon_irreversible_climate_change-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Even if emissions were drastically reduced, global temperatures would remain close to their highest level for at least 1,000 years (see the later section on\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Irreversibilities" title="Effects of global warming">\n        irreversibilities\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Projected_warming_in_context">\n        Projected warming in context\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <div class="thumb tright">\n          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png">\n            <img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="600" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png/250px-2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png/375px-2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png/500px-2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png 2x" width="250"/>\n           </a>\n           <div class="thumbcaption">\n            <div class="magnify">\n             <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2000_Year_Temperature_Comparison.png" title="Enlarge">\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            Two millennia of mean surface temperatures according to different reconstructions from\n            <a href="/wiki/Proxy_(climate)" title="Proxy (climate)">\n             climate proxies\n            </a>\n            , each smoothed on a decadal scale, with the\n            <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_temperature_record" title="Instrumental temperature record">\n             instrumental temperature record\n            </a>\n            overlaid in black.\n           </div>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <div class="thumb tright">\n          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature,_based_on_ocean_cores_(NASA).png">\n            <img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1888" data-file-width="3486" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature%2C_based_on_ocean_cores_%28NASA%29.png/250px-Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature%2C_based_on_ocean_cores_%28NASA%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature%2C_based_on_ocean_cores_%28NASA%29.png/375px-Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature%2C_based_on_ocean_cores_%28NASA%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature%2C_based_on_ocean_cores_%28NASA%29.png/500px-Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature%2C_based_on_ocean_cores_%28NASA%29.png 2x" width="250"/>\n           </a>\n           <div class="thumbcaption">\n            <div class="magnify">\n             <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Global_temperature_relative_to_peak_Holocene_temperature,_based_on_ocean_cores_(NASA).png" title="Enlarge">\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            Global surface temperature for the past 5.3 million years as inferred from cores of ocean\n            <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">\n             sediments\n            </a>\n            taken all around the global ocean. The last 800,000 years are expanded in the lower half of the figure (image credit:\n            <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n             NASA\n            </a>\n            ).\n            <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hansen_climate_history_35-0">\n             <a href="#cite_note-hansen_climate_history-35">\n              [35]\n             </a>\n            </sup>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Scientists have used various "proxy" data to assess past changes in Earth\'s climate (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paleoclimate" title="Paleoclimate">\n        paleoclimate\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaa_proxy_climate_data_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-noaa_proxy_climate_data-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sources of proxy data include historical records (such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Farmer" title="Farmer">\n        farmers\n       </a>\n       \' logs),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tree_ring" title="Tree ring">\n        tree rings\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">\n        corals\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_pollen" title="Fossil pollen">\n        fossil pollen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_core" title="Ice core">\n        ice cores\n       </a>\n       , and ocean and lake\n       <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">\n        sediments\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaa_proxy_climate_data_36-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-noaa_proxy_climate_data-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Analysis of these data suggest that recent warming is unusual in the past 400 years, possibly longer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By the end of the 21st century, temperatures may increase to a level not experienced since the mid-\n       <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">\n        Pliocene\n       </a>\n       , around 3 million years ago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jansen_pliocene_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jansen_pliocene-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At that time, models suggest that mean global temperatures were about 2\xe2\x80\x933\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C warmer than pre-industrial temperatures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jansen_pliocene_38-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jansen_pliocene-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Even a 2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C rise above the pre-industrial level would be outside the range of temperatures experienced by human\n       <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">\n        civilization\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hansen_climate_history_35-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hansen_climate_history-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_impacts">\n        Physical impacts\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Physical_impacts_of_climate_change" title="Physical impacts of climate change">\n        Physical impacts of climate change\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <div class="thumb tright">\n          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png">\n            <img alt="Refer to caption and adjacent text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1691" data-file-width="3191" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png/450px-Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png/675px-Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png/900px-Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png 2x" width="450"/>\n           </a>\n           <div class="thumbcaption">\n            <div class="magnify">\n             <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png" title="Enlarge">\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            Seven of these indicators would be expected to increase in a warming world and observations show that they are, in fact, increasing. Three would be expected to decrease and they are, in fact, decreasing.\n            <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n             <a href="#cite_note-40">\n              [40]\n             </a>\n            </sup>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png">\n         <img alt="Refer to caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3242" data-file-width="2100" height="540" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png/350px-Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png/525px-Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png/700px-Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         This set of graphs show changes in climate indicators over several decades. Each of the different colored lines in each panel represents an independently analyzed set of data. The data come from many different technologies including\n         <a href="/wiki/Weather_station" title="Weather station">\n          weather stations\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">\n          satellites\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weather_balloons" title="Weather balloons">\n          weather balloons\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Ship" title="Ship">\n          ships\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Buoy" title="Buoy">\n          buoys\n         </a>\n         .\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n          <a href="#cite_note-41">\n           [41]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A broad range of evidence shows that the climate system has warmed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Evidence of global warming is shown in the graphs opposite. Some of the graphs show a positive\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trend_estimation" title="Trend estimation">\n        trend\n       </a>\n       , e.g., increasing temperature over land and the ocean, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_sea_level_rise" title="Current sea level rise">\n        sea level rise\n       </a>\n       . Other graphs show a negative trend, e.g., decreased\n       <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">\n        snow\n       </a>\n       cover in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">\n        Northern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       , and declining\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_sea_ice" title="Arctic sea ice">\n        Arctic sea ice\n       </a>\n       extent. Evidence of warming is also apparent in living\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Observed_impacts_on_biological_systems" title="Effects of global warming">\n        (biological) systems\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Human activities have contributed to a number of the observed changes in climate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hegerl_climate_change_attribution_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hegerl_climate_change_attribution-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This contribution has principally been through the burning of\n       <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">\n        fossil fuels\n       </a>\n       , which has led to an increase in the concentration of GHGs in the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another human influence on the climate are\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">\n        sulfur dioxide\n       </a>\n       emissions, which are a precursor to the formation of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sulfate_aerosols" title="Sulfate aerosols">\n        sulfate aerosols\n       </a>\n       in the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Human-induced warming could lead to\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Abrupt_or_irreversible_changes" title="Effects of global warming">\n        large-scale, irreversible, and/or abrupt changes\n       </a>\n       in physical systems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An example of this is the melting of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_sheet" title="Ice sheet">\n        ice sheets\n       </a>\n       , which contributes to sea level rise.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magnitudes_of_impact_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-magnitudes_of_impact-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The probability of warming having unforeseen consequences increases with the rate, magnitude, and duration of climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_weather">\n        Effects on weather\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Observations show that there have been changes in weather.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As climate changes, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Probabilities" title="Probabilities">\n        probabilities\n       </a>\n       of certain types of weather events are affected.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century,_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario,_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png">\n         <img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png/250px-Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png/375px-Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png/500px-Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century,_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario,_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Projected change in annual average precipitation by the end of the 21st century, based on a medium emissions scenario (\n         <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">\n          SRES\n         </a>\n         A1B) (Credit: NOAA\n         <a href="/wiki/Geophysical_Fluid_Dynamics_Laboratory" title="Geophysical Fluid Dynamics Laboratory">\n          Geophysical Fluid Dynamics Laboratory\n         </a>\n         ).\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n          <a href="#cite_note-52">\n           [52]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">\n           [53]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Changes have been observed in the amount, intensity, frequency, and type of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">\n        precipitation\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :18\n       </sup>\n       Widespread increases in heavy precipitation have occurred, even in places where total rain amounts have decreased. With medium confidence (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Footnotes" title="Effects of global warming">\n        footnote 1\n       </a>\n       ), IPCC (2012)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       concluded that human influences had contributed to an increase in heavy precipitation events at the global scale.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Projections of future changes in precipitation show overall increases in the global average, but with substantial shifts in where and how precipitation falls.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :24\n       </sup>\n       Projections suggest a reduction in rainfall in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">\n        subtropics\n       </a>\n       , and an increase in precipitation in subpolar latitudes and some\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equatorial_region" title="Equatorial region">\n        equatorial regions\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In other words, regions which are dry at present will in general become even drier, while regions that are currently wet will in general become even wetter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This projection does not apply to every locale, and in some cases can be modified by local conditions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_weather">\n        Extreme weather\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">\n        Extreme weather\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Global_warming" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        Tropical cyclone \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Global warming\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Over most land areas since the 1950s, it is very likely that there have been fewer or warmer cold days and nights.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hot days and nights have also very likely become warmer or more frequent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Human activities have very likely contributed to these trends.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There may have been changes in other climate extremes (e.g.,\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">\n        floods\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">\n        droughts\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       ) but these changes are more difficult to identify.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Projections suggest changes in the frequency and intensity of some extreme weather events.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Confidence in projections varies over time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Near-term projections (2016\xe2\x80\x932035)\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Some changes (e.g., more frequent hot days) will probably be evident in the near term, while other near-term changes (e.g., more intense droughts and tropical cyclones) are more uncertain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Long-term projections (2081\xe2\x80\x932100)\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Future climate change will be associated with more very hot days and fewer very cold days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The frequency, length and intensity of\n       <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">\n        heat waves\n       </a>\n       will very likely increase over most land areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Higher growth in anthropogenic GHG emissions will be associated with larger increases in the frequency and severity of temperature extremes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Assuming high growth in GHG emissions (IPCC scenario\n       <a href="/wiki/Representative_Concentration_Pathways" title="Representative Concentration Pathways">\n        RCP8.5\n       </a>\n       ), presently dry regions may be affected by an increase in the risk of drought and reductions in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soil_moisture" title="Soil moisture">\n        soil moisture\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over most of the mid-latitude land masses and wet tropical regions, extreme precipitation events will very likely become more intense and frequent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Tropical cyclones\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       At the global scale, the frequency of tropical cyclones will probably decrease or be unchanged.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christensen_2013_cyclones_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-christensen_2013_cyclones-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Global mean tropical cyclone maximum wind speed and precipitation rates will likely increase.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christensen_2013_cyclones_58-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-christensen_2013_cyclones-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Changes in tropical cyclones will probably vary by region, but these variations are uncertain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christensen_2013_cyclones_58-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-christensen_2013_cyclones-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Effects of climate extremes\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The impacts of extreme events on the environment and human society will vary. Some impacts will be beneficial\xe2\x80\x94e.g., fewer cold extremes will probably lead to fewer cold deaths.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health_summary_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-health_summary-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overall, however, impacts will probably be mostly negative.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar4_synthesis_reasons_for_concern_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar4_synthesis_reasons_for_concern-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cryosphere">\n        Cryosphere\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">\n        Retreat of glaciers since 1850\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png">\n         <img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="650" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png/220px-Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png/330px-Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png/440px-Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A map of the change in thickness of mountain glaciers since 1970. Thinning in orange and red, thickening in blue.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg">\n         <img alt="2012 Arctic sea ice extent" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="770" data-file-width="1440" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg/220px-SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg/330px-SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg/440px-SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A map that shows ice concentration on 16 September 2012, along with the extent of the previous record low (yellow line) and the mid-September median extent (black line) setting a new record low that was 18 percent smaller than the previous record and nearly 50 percent smaller than the long-term (1979\xe2\x80\x932000) average.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Cryosphere" title="Cryosphere">\n        cryosphere\n       </a>\n       is made up of areas of the Earth which are covered by snow or ice.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Observed changes in the cryosphere include declines in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_sea_ice" title="Arctic sea ice">\n        Arctic sea ice\n       </a>\n       extent,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the widespread retreat of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpine_glaciers" title="Alpine glaciers">\n        alpine glaciers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and reduced snow cover in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">\n        Northern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Solomon\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar4_arctic_sea_ice_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar4_arctic_sea_ice-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       assessed the potential impacts of climate change on\n       <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">\n        summertime\n       </a>\n       Arctic sea ice extent. Assuming high growth in greenhouse gas emissions (\n       <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">\n        SRES A2\n       </a>\n       ), some models projected that Arctic sea ice in the summer could largely disappear by the end of the 21st century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar4_arctic_sea_ice_66-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar4_arctic_sea_ice-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       More recent projections suggest that the Arctic summers could be ice-free (defined as ice extent less than 1 million square km) as early as 2025\xe2\x80\x932030.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the 21st century, glaciers\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and snow cover are projected to continue their widespread retreat.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the western mountains of\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       , increasing temperatures and changes in precipitation are projected to lead to reduced\n       <a href="/wiki/Snowpack" title="Snowpack">\n        snowpack\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Snowpack is the seasonal accumulation of slow-melting snow.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The melting of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland_ice_sheet" title="Greenland ice sheet">\n        Greenland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Antarctic_ice_sheet" title="West Antarctic ice sheet">\n        West Antarctic ice sheets\n       </a>\n       could contribute to sea level rise, especially over long time-scales (see the section on\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Greenland_and_West_Antarctic_Ice_sheets" title="Effects of global warming">\n        Greenland and West Antarctic Ice sheets\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magnitudes_of_impact_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-magnitudes_of_impact-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Changes in the cryosphere are projected to have social impacts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, in some regions, glacier retreat could increase the risk of reductions in seasonal water availability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Barnett\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2005)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       estimated that more than one-sixth of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_population" title="World\'s population">\n        world\'s population\n       </a>\n       rely on glaciers and snowpack for their water supply.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Oceans">\n        Oceans\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming_on_oceans" title="Effects of global warming on oceans">\n        Effects of global warming on oceans\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The role of the oceans in global warming is complex. The oceans serve as a sink for carbon dioxide, taking up much that would otherwise remain in the atmosphere, but increased levels of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       have led to\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">\n        ocean acidification\n       </a>\n       . Furthermore, as the temperature of the oceans increases, they become less able to absorb excess\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       . The ocean have also acted as a sink in absorbing extra heat from the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statecl_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-statecl-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :4\n       </sup>\n       The increase in ocean\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heat_content" title="Heat content">\n        heat content\n       </a>\n       is much larger than any other store of\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       in the Earth\xe2\x80\x99s heat balance over the two periods 1961 to 2003 and 1993 to 2003, and accounts for more than 90% of the possible increase in heat content of the Earth system during these periods.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Global warming is projected to have a number of effects on the oceans. Ongoing effects include rising sea levels due to thermal expansion and melting of glaciers and ice sheets, and warming of the ocean surface, leading to increased temperature stratification. Other possible effects include large-scale changes in ocean circulation.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Acidification">\n        Acidification\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">\n        Ocean acidification\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans,_1880-2012_(US_EPA).png">\n         <img alt="refer to caption and image description" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="536" data-file-width="670" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png/220px-Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png/330px-Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png/440px-Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans,_1880-2012_(US_EPA).png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         This map shows changes in the amount of\n         <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">\n          aragonite\n         </a>\n         dissolved in\n         <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">\n          ocean\n         </a>\n         surface waters between the 1880s and the most recent decade (2003\xe2\x80\x932012).\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">\n           [77]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         Historical modeling suggests that since the 1880s, increased CO\n         <sub>\n          2\n         </sub>\n         has led to lower\n         <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">\n          aragonite\n         </a>\n         saturation levels (less availability of minerals) in the oceans around the world.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">\n           [77]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         The largest decreases in aragonite saturation have occurred in\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">\n          tropical\n         </a>\n         waters.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">\n           [77]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         However, decreases in cold areas may be of greater concern because colder waters typically have lower aragonite levels to begin with.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">\n           [77]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       About one-third of the carbon dioxide emitted by human activity has already been taken up by the oceans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As carbon dioxide dissolves in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_water" title="Sea water">\n        sea water\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbonic_acid" title="Carbonic acid">\n        carbonic acid\n       </a>\n       is formed, which has the effect of acidifying the ocean, measured as a change in\n       <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">\n        pH\n       </a>\n       . The uptake of human carbon emissions since the year 1750 has led to an average decrease in pH of 0.1 units.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Projections using the SRES emissions scenarios suggest a further reduction in average global surface ocean pH of between 0.14 and 0.35 units over the 21st century.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The effects of ocean acidification on the marine\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">\n        biosphere\n       </a>\n       have yet to be documented.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification_79-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Laboratory experiments suggest beneficial effects for a few species, with potentially highly detrimental effects for a substantial number of species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification_78-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With medium confidence, Fischlin\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       projected that future ocean acidification and climate change would impair a wide range of\n       <a href="/wiki/Plankton" title="Plankton">\n        planktonic\n       </a>\n       and shallow\n       <a href="/wiki/Benthos" title="Benthos">\n        benthic\n       </a>\n       marine organisms that use\n       <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">\n        aragonite\n       </a>\n       to make their shells or skeletons, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">\n        corals\n       </a>\n       and marine\n       <a href="/wiki/Snail" title="Snail">\n        snails\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Pteropoda" title="Pteropoda">\n        pteropods\n       </a>\n       ), with significant impacts particularly in the Southern Ocean.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Oxygen_depletion">\n        Oxygen depletion\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The amount of oxygen dissolved in the oceans may decline, with adverse consequences for ocean life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sea_level_rise">\n        Sea level rise\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_sea_level_rise" title="Current sea level rise">\n        Current sea level rise\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Future_sea_level" title="Future sea level">\n        Future sea level\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level,_1870-2008_(US_EPA).png">\n         <img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="670" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png/220px-Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png/330px-Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png/440px-Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level,_1870-2008_(US_EPA).png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Trends in global average absolute sea level, 1870\xe2\x80\x932008.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n          <a href="#cite_note-83">\n           [83]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There is strong evidence that global sea level rose gradually over the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With high confidence, Bindoff\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n
