<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       concluded that between the mid-19th and mid-20th centuries, the rate of sea level rise increased. Authors of the IPCC Fourth Assessment Synthesis Report (IPCC AR4 SYR, 2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       reported that between the years 1961 and 2003, global average sea level rose at an average rate of 1.8\xc2\xa0mm per year (mm/yr), with a range of 1.3\xe2\x80\x932.3\xc2\xa0mm/yr. Between 1993 and 2003, the rate increased above the previous period to 3.1\xc2\xa0mm/yr (range of 2.4\xe2\x80\x933.8\xc2\xa0mm/yr). Authors of IPCC AR4 SYR (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects_21-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       were uncertain whether the increase in rate from 1993 to 2003 was due to\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change#Internal_forcing_mechanisms" title="Climate change">\n        natural variations\n       </a>\n       in sea level over the time period, or whether it reflected an increase in the underlying long-term trend.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are two main factors that have contributed to observed sea level rise.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising_84-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first is\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_expansion" title="Thermal expansion">\n        thermal expansion\n       </a>\n       : as ocean water warms, it expands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The second is from the contribution of land-based ice due to increased melting. The major store of water on land is found in glaciers and ice sheets. Anthropogenic forces very likely (greater than 90% probability, based on expert judgement)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       contributed to sea level rise during the latter half of the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hegerl_climate_change_attribution_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hegerl_climate_change_attribution-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is a widespread consensus that substantial long-term sea level rise will continue for centuries to come.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In their Fourth Assessment Report, the IPCC\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       projected sea level rise to the end of the 21st century using the SRES emissions scenarios. Across the six SRES marker scenarios, sea level was projected to rise by 18 to 59\xc2\xa0cm (7.1 to 23.2\xc2\xa0in), relative to sea level at the end of the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Thermal expansion is the largest component in these projections, contributing 70\xe2\x80\x9375% of the central estimate for all scenarios.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Due to a lack of scientific understanding, this sea level rise estimate does not include all of the possible contributions of ice sheets (see the section on\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Greenland_and_West_Antarctic_Ice_sheets" title="Effects of global warming">\n        Greenland and West Antarctic Ice sheets\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An assessment of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_literature" title="Scientific literature">\n        scientific literature\n       </a>\n       on climate change was published in 2010 by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_National_Research_Council" title="US National Research Council">\n        US National Research Council\n       </a>\n       (US NRC, 2010).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NRC (2010)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       described the projections in AR4 (i.e. those cited in the above paragraph) as "conservative", and summarized the results of more recent studies. Cited studies suggested a great deal of uncertainty in projections.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A range of projections suggested possible sea level rise by the end of the 21st century of between 0.56 and 2 m, relative to sea levels at the end of the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ocean_temperature_rise">\n        Ocean temperature rise\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heat_content700m2000myr.png">\n         <img alt="Global ocean heat content" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="566" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Heat_content700m2000myr.png/220px-Heat_content700m2000myr.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Heat_content700m2000myr.png/330px-Heat_content700m2000myr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Heat_content700m2000myr.png/440px-Heat_content700m2000myr.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heat_content700m2000myr.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Global ocean heat content from 1955\xe2\x80\x932012\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       From 1961 to 2003, the global ocean temperature has risen by 0.10\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C from the surface to a depth of 700 m. There is variability both year-to-year and over longer time scales, with global ocean heat content observations showing high rates of warming for 1991\xe2\x80\x932003, but some cooling from 2003 to 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The temperature of the Antarctic\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">\n        Southern Ocean\n       </a>\n       rose by 0.17\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (0.31\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) between the 1950s and the 1980s, nearly twice the rate for the world\'s oceans as a whole.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As well as having effects on ecosystems (e.g. by melting sea ice, affecting algae that grow on its underside), warming reduces the ocean\'s ability to absorb\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       It is likely (greater than 66% probability, based on expert judgement)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       that anthropogenic forcing contributed to the general warming observed in the upper several hundred metres of the ocean during the latter half of the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hegerl_climate_change_attribution_44-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hegerl_climate_change_attribution-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">\n        Regions\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Regional_effects_of_global_warming" title="Regional effects of global warming">\n        Regional effects of global warming\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_(left)_and_the_1980s_(right),_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_(US_EPA).jpg">\n           <img srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg/450px-Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg compared to average temperatures from 1951 to 1980.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n           <a href="#cite_note-94">\n            [94]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_(2007).jpg">\n           <img alt="Future warming across the globe varies according to different projections of greenhouse gas emissions" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="720" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg/300px-Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg/450px-Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg/600px-Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Projected changes in average temperatures across the world in the 2050s under three greenhouse gas (GHG)\n          <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_global_warming#Emissions_scenarios" title="Economics of global warming">\n           emissions scenarios\n          </a>\n          .\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-herring_temperature_projections_19-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-herring_temperature_projections-19">\n            [19]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Regional effects of global warming vary in nature. Some are the result of a generalised global change, such as rising temperature, resulting in local effects, such as melting ice. In other cases, a change may be related to a change in a particular ocean current or weather system. In such cases, the regional effect may be disproportionate and will not necessarily follow the global trend.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are three major ways in which global warming will make changes to regional climate: melting or forming ice, changing the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrological_cycle" title="Hydrological cycle">\n        hydrological cycle\n       </a>\n       (of\n       <a href="/wiki/Evaporation" title="Evaporation">\n        evaporation\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">\n        precipitation\n       </a>\n       ) and changing\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_current" title="Ocean current">\n        currents in the oceans\n       </a>\n       and air flows in the atmosphere. The coast can also be considered a region, and will suffer severe impacts from\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">\n        sea level rise\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Observed_impacts">\n        Observed impacts\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       With very high confidence, Rosenzweig\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       concluded that physical and biological systems on all continents and in most oceans had been affected by recent climate changes, particularly regional temperature increases. Impacts include earlier leafing of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tree" title="Tree">\n        trees\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">\n        plants\n       </a>\n       over many regions; movements of species to higher latitudes and altitudes in the Northern Hemisphere; changes in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">\n        bird migrations\n       </a>\n       in Europe, North America and Australia; and shifting of the oceans\'\n       <a href="/wiki/Plankton" title="Plankton">\n        plankton\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">\n        fish\n       </a>\n       from cold- to warm-adapted communities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_briefs_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa_briefs-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The human influence on the climate can be seen in the geographical pattern of observed warming, with greater temperature increases over land and in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_region" title="Polar region">\n        polar regions\n       </a>\n       rather than over the oceans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure_96-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :6\n       </sup>\n       Using models, it is possible to identify the human "signal" of global warming over both land and ocean areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure_96-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :6\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Projected_impacts">\n        Projected impacts\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Projections of future climate changes at the regional scale do not hold as high a level of scientific confidence as projections made at the global scale.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure_96-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :9\n       </sup>\n       It is, however, expected that future warming will follow a similar geographical pattern to that seen already, with greatest warming over land and high northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitudes\n       </a>\n       , and least over the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">\n        Southern Ocean\n       </a>\n       and parts of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="North Atlantic Ocean">\n        North Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nearly all land areas will very likely warm more than the global average.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tar_table_of_robust_findings_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tar_table_of_robust_findings-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">\n        Arctic\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">\n        Africa\n       </a>\n       , small islands and\n       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">\n        Asian\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">\n        megadeltas\n       </a>\n       are regions that are likely to be especially affected by climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar4_especially_affected_regions_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar4_especially_affected_regions-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">\n        Low-latitude\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">\n        less-developed\n       </a>\n       areas are at most risk of experiencing negative impacts due to climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_distribution_of_impacts_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_distribution_of_impacts-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries">\n        Developed countries\n       </a>\n       are also vulnerable to climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, developed countries will be negatively affected by increases in the severity and frequency of some\n       <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">\n        extreme weather\n       </a>\n       events, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">\n        heat waves\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities_101-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In all regions, some people can be particularly at risk from climate change, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">\n        poor\n       </a>\n       , young\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Children" title="Children">\n        children\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elderly" title="Elderly">\n        elderly\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar4_especially_affected_regions_99-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar4_especially_affected_regions-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_distribution_of_impacts_100-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_distribution_of_impacts-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_systems">\n        Social systems\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_humans" title="Effects of climate change on humans">\n        Effects of climate change on humans\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change,_industry_and_society" title="Climate change, industry and society">\n        Climate change, industry and society\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_gender" title="Climate change and gender">\n        Climate change and gender\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The impacts of climate change can be thought of in terms of sensitivity and vulnerability. "Sensitivity" is the degree to which a particular system or sector might be affected, positively or negatively, by climate change and/or\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change#Causes" title="Climate change">\n        climate variability\n       </a>\n       . "Vulnerability" is the degree to which a particular system or sector might be adversely affected by climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The sensitivity of human society to climate change varies. Sectors sensitive to climate change include water resources, coastal zones, human settlements, and human health. Industries sensitive to climate change include\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_agriculture" title="Climate change and agriculture">\n        agriculture\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fisheries_and_climate_change" title="Fisheries and climate change">\n        fisheries\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">\n        forestry\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy_industry" title="Energy industry">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">\n        construction\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">\n        insurance\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">\n        financial services\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">\n        tourism\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">\n        recreation\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Food_supply">\n        Food supply\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_agriculture" title="Climate change and agriculture">\n        Climate change and agriculture\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">\n        Food security\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_vs_fuel" title="Food vs fuel">\n        Food vs fuel\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_world_food_price_crisis" title="2007\xe2\x80\x932008 world food price crisis">\n        2007\xe2\x80\x932008 world food price crisis\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1074" data-file-width="1448" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png/220px-Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png/330px-Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png/440px-Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Graph of net crop production worldwide and in selected tropical countries. Raw data from the United Nations.\n         <a class="external autonumber" href="http://faostat3.fao.org/browse/Q/QC/E" rel="nofollow">\n          [2]\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Climate change will impact agriculture and food production around the world due to: the effects of elevated CO\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       in the atmosphere, higher temperatures, altered precipitation and\n       <a href="/wiki/Transpiration" title="Transpiration">\n        transpiration\n       </a>\n       regimes, increased frequency of extreme events, and modified\n       <a href="/wiki/Weed" title="Weed">\n        weed\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">\n        pest\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">\n        pathogen\n       </a>\n       pressure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In general, low-latitude areas are at most risk of having decreased crop yields.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2007, the effects of regional climate change on agriculture have been small.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Changes in crop\n       <a href="/wiki/Phenology" title="Phenology">\n        phenology\n       </a>\n       provide important evidence of the response to recent regional climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Phenology is the study of natural phenomena that recur periodically, and how these phenomena relate to climate and seasonal changes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A significant advance in phenology has been observed for agriculture and forestry in large parts of the Northern Hemisphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Projections">\n        Projections\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png">\n         <img alt="Refer to caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="694" data-file-width="1322" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png/350px-Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png/525px-Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png/700px-Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Projected changes in crop yields at different latitudes with global warming. This graph is based on several studies.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1_110-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1-110">\n           [110]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png">\n         <img alt="Refer to caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="689" data-file-width="1345" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png/350px-Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png/525px-Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png/700px-Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Projected changes in yields of selected crops with global warming. This graph is based on several studies.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1_110-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1-110">\n           [110]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       With low to medium confidence, Schneider\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-table_of_key_vulnerabilities_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-table_of_key_vulnerabilities-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       projected that for about a 1 to 3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C increase in global mean temperature (by the years 2090\xe2\x80\x932100, relative to average temperatures in the years 1990\xe2\x80\x932000), there would be productivity decreases for some\n       <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">\n        cereals\n       </a>\n       in low latitudes, and productivity increases in high latitudes. With medium confidence, global production potential was projected to:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-table_of_key_vulnerabilities_20-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-table_of_key_vulnerabilities-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        increase up to around 3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C,\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        very likely decrease above about 3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Most of the studies on global agriculture assessed by Schneider\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture_107-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       had not incorporated a number of critical factors, including changes in extreme events, or the spread of pests and diseases. Studies had also not considered the development of specific practices or technologies to aid\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adaptation_to_global_warming#Agricultural_production" title="Adaptation to global warming">\n        adaptation to climate change\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture_107-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The graphs opposite show the projected effects of climate change on selected crop yields.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2011_text_111-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2011_text-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Actual changes in yields may be above or below these central estimates.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2011_text_111-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2011_text-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The projections above can be expressed relative to pre-industrial (1750) temperatures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       0.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C of warming is estimated to have occurred between 1750 and 1990\xe2\x80\x932000. Add 0.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C to the above projections to convert them from a 1990\xe2\x80\x932000 to pre-industrial baseline.\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Food_security">\n        Food security\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <p>\n       Easterling\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       assessed studies that made quantitative projections of climate change impacts on\n       <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">\n        food security\n       </a>\n       . It was noted that these projections were highly uncertain and had limitations. However, the assessed studies suggested a number of fairly robust findings. The first was that climate change would likely increase the number of people at risk of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">\n        hunger\n       </a>\n       compared with reference scenarios with no climate change. Climate change impacts depended strongly on projected future social and economic development. Additionally, the magnitude of climate change impacts was projected to be smaller compared to the impact of social and economic development. In 2006, the global estimate for the number of people\n       <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">\n        undernourished\n       </a>\n       was 820 million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Under the SRES A1, B1, and B2 scenarios (see the\n       <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios#Scenario_families" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">\n        SRES article\n       </a>\n       for information on each scenario group), projections for the year 2080 showed a reduction in the number of people undernourished of about 560\xe2\x80\x93700\xc2\xa0million people, with a global total of undernourished people of 100\xe2\x80\x93240\xc2\xa0million in 2080. By contrast, the SRES A2 scenario showed only a small decrease in the risk of hunger from 2006 levels. The smaller reduction under A2 was attributed to the higher projected future population level in this scenario.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Droughts_and_agriculture">\n        Droughts and agriculture\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Some evidence suggests that droughts have been occurring more frequently because of global warming and they are expected to become more frequent and intense in Africa, southern Europe, the Middle East, most of the Americas, Australia, and Southeast Asia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, other research suggests that there has been little change in drought over the past 60 years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Their impacts are aggravated because of increased water demand, population growth, urban expansion, and environmental protection efforts in many areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n        <a href="#cite_note-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Droughts result in crop failures and the loss of pasture grazing land for livestock.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">\n        Health\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming_on_human_health" title="Effects of global warming on human health">\n        Effects of global warming on human health\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Human beings are exposed to climate change through changing weather patterns (temperature, precipitation, sea-level rise and more frequent extreme events) and indirectly through changes in water, air and food quality and changes in ecosystems, agriculture, industry and settlements and the economy (Confalonieri\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       , 2007:393).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health_summary_59-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-health_summary-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to an assessment of the scientific literature by Confalonieri\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007:393),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health_summary_59-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-health_summary-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the effects of climate change to date have been small, but are projected to progressively increase in all countries and regions.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A study by the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">\n        World Health Organization\n       </a>\n       (WHO, 2009)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       estimated the effect of climate change on human health. Not all of the effects of climate change were included in their estimates, for example, the effects of more frequent and extreme storms were excluded. Climate change was estimated to have been responsible for 3% of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diarrhoea" title="Diarrhoea">\n        diarrhoea\n       </a>\n       , 3% of\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">\n        malaria\n       </a>\n       , and 3.8% of\n       <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">\n        dengue fever\n       </a>\n       deaths worldwide in 2004. Total attributable mortality was about 0.2% of deaths in 2004; of these, 85% were child deaths.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Projections_2">\n        Projections\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       With high confidence, authors of the IPCC AR4 Synthesis report\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR4_Synthesis_Report_120-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR4_Synthesis_Report-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :48\n       </sup>\n       projected that climate change would bring some benefits in temperate areas, such as fewer deaths from cold exposure, and some mixed effects such as changes in range and transmission potential of\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">\n        malaria\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">\n        Africa\n       </a>\n       . Benefits were projected to be outweighed by negative health effects of rising temperatures, especially in developing countries.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With very high confidence, Confalonieri\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health_summary_59-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-health_summary-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :393\n       </sup>\n       concluded that economic development was an important component of possible adaptation to climate change. Economic growth on its own, however, was not judged to be sufficient to insulate the world\'s population from disease and injury due to climate change. Future vulnerability to climate change will depend not only on the extent of social and economic change, but also on how the benefits and costs of change are distributed in society.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Future_vulnerability_to_climate_change_health_impacts_121-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Future_vulnerability_to_climate_change_health_impacts-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, in the 19th century, rapid\n       <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">\n        urbanization\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">\n        western Europe\n       </a>\n       lead to a plummeting in population health.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Future_vulnerability_to_climate_change_health_impacts_121-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Future_vulnerability_to_climate_change_health_impacts-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other factors important in determining the health of populations include\n       <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">\n        education\n       </a>\n       , the availability of health services, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">\n        public-health\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">\n        infrastructure\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health_summary_59-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-health_summary-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :393\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_resources">\n        Water resources\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_security" title="Water security">\n        Water security\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg">\n         <img alt="refer to caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="959" data-file-width="649" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg/220px-NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg/330px-NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg/440px-NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NOAAprecipitationtrend.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Precipitation during the 20th century and up through 2008 during global warming, the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">\n          NOAA\n         </a>\n         estimating an observed trend over that period of 1.87% global precipitation increase per century.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A number of climate-related trends have been observed that affect\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_resources" title="Water resources">\n        water resources\n       </a>\n       . These include changes in precipitation, the crysosphere and\n       <a href="/wiki/Surface_water" title="Surface water">\n        surface waters\n       </a>\n       (e.g., changes in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_flows" title="River flows">\n        river flows\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Observed and projected impacts of climate change on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">\n        freshwater\n       </a>\n       systems and their management are mainly due to changes in temperature, sea level and precipitation variability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freshwater_impacts_123-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-freshwater_impacts-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sea level rise will extend areas of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salinization" title="Salinization">\n        salinization\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">\n        groundwater\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">\n        estuaries\n       </a>\n       , resulting in a decrease in freshwater availability for humans and ecosystems in coastal areas. In an assessment of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_literature" title="Scientific literature">\n        scientific literature\n       </a>\n       , Kundzewicz\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freshwater_impacts_123-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-freshwater_impacts-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       concluded, with high confidence, that:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        the negative impacts of climate change on freshwater systems outweigh the benefits. All of the regions assessed in the\n        <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">\n         IPCC Fourth Assessment Report\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">\n         Africa\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">\n         Asia\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n         Australia\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">\n         New Zealand\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">\n         Europe\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">\n         Latin America\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n         North America\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_region" title="Polar region">\n         Polar regions\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">\n         Arctic\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">\n         Antarctic\n        </a>\n        ), and small islands) showed an overall net negative impact of climate change on water resources and freshwater ecosystems.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">\n         Semi-arid\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">\n         arid\n        </a>\n        areas are particularly exposed to the impacts of climate change on freshwater. With very high confidence, it was judged that many of these areas, e.g., the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean_basin" title="Mediterranean basin">\n         Mediterranean basin\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Western_United_States" title="Western United States">\n         Western United States\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">\n         Southern Africa\n        </a>\n        , and north-eastern\n        <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">\n         Brazil\n        </a>\n        , would suffer a decrease in water resources due to climate change.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Migration_and_conflict">\n        Migration and conflict\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_migrant" title="Environmental migrant">\n        Environmental migrant\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_climate_model" title="Global climate model">\n        General circulation models\n       </a>\n       project that the future climate change will bring wetter coasts, drier mid-continent areas, and further sea level rise.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sar_migration_124-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sar_migration-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Such changes could result in the gravest effects of climate change through\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">\n        human migration\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Millions might be displaced by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shoreline_erosion" title="Shoreline erosion">\n        shoreline erosions\n       </a>\n       , river and coastal\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">\n        flooding\n       </a>\n       , or severe\n       <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">\n        drought\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Migration related to climate change is likely to be predominantly from\n       <a href="/wiki/Rural_area" title="Rural area">\n        rural areas\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">\n        developing countries\n       </a>\n       to towns and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities" title="Cities">\n        cities\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sar_migration_124-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sar_migration-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :407\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wdr_migration_126-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wdr_migration-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the short term climate stress is likely to add incrementally to existing migration patterns rather than generating entirely new flows of people.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wdr_migration_126-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wdr_migration-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :110\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It has been argued that environmental degradation, loss of access to resources (e.g., water resources),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and resulting human migration could become a source of political and even\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_conflict" title="Military conflict">\n        military conflict\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tar_migration_128-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tar_migration-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Factors other than climate change may, however, be more important in affecting conflict. For example, Wilbanks\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       suggested that major environmentally influenced conflicts in Africa were more to do with the relative abundance of resources, e.g.,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">\n        oil\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">\n        diamonds\n       </a>\n       , than with resource scarcity. Scott\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2001) placed only low confidence in predictions of increased conflict due to climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tar_migration_128-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tar_migration-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A 2013 study found that significant climatic changes were associated with a higher risk of conflict worldwide, and predicted that "amplified rates of human conflict could represent a large and critical social impact of anthropogenic climate change in both low- and high-income countries."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Similarly, a 2014 study found that higher temperatures were associated with a greater likelihood of violent crime, and predicted that global warming would cause millions of such crimes in the United States alone during the 21st century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Military planners are concerned that global warming is a "threat multiplier". "Whether it is poverty, food and\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">\n        water scarcity\n       </a>\n       , diseases, economic instability, or threat of natural disasters, the broad range of changing climatic conditions may be far reaching. These challenges may threaten stability in much of the world".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Aggregate_impacts">\n        Aggregate impacts\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Economic_impacts_of_climate_change" title="Economic impacts of climate change">\n        Economic impacts of climate change\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Aggregate_data" title="Aggregate data">\n        Aggregating\n       </a>\n       impacts adds up the total impact of climate change across sectors and/or regions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Examples of aggregate measures include\n       <a href="/wiki/Economic_impacts_of_climate_change#Distribution_of_impacts" title="Economic impacts of climate change">\n        economic cost\n       </a>\n       (e.g., changes in\n       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">\n        gross domestic product\n       </a>\n       (GDP) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Economic_impacts_of_climate_change#Marginal_impacts" title="Economic impacts of climate change">\n        social cost of carbon\n       </a>\n       ), changes in ecosystems (e.g., changes over land area from one type of vegetation to another),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       human health impacts, and the number of people affected by climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Aggregate measures such as economic cost require researchers to make\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Value_judgement" title="Value judgement">\n        value judgements\n       </a>\n       over the importance of impacts occurring in different regions and at different times.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Observed_impacts_2">\n        Observed impacts\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Global losses reveal rapidly rising costs due to extreme weather-related events since the 1970s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomics" title="Socioeconomics">\n        Socio-economic\n       </a>\n       factors have contributed to the observed trend of global losses, e.g., population growth, increased\n       <a href="/wiki/Wealth" title="Wealth">\n        wealth\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disaster_losses_137-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disaster_losses-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Part of the growth is also related to regional climatic factors, e.g., changes in precipitation and flooding events. It is difficult to quantify the relative impact of socio-economic factors and climate change on the observed trend.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disaster_losses_137-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disaster_losses-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The trend does, however, suggest increasing vulnerability of social systems to climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disaster_losses_137-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-disaster_losses-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Projected_impacts_2">\n        Projected impacts\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The total economic impacts from climate change are highly uncertain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With medium confidence, Smith\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2001)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_estimate_of_climate_change_impacts_on_GDP_140-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Smith_estimate_of_climate_change_impacts_on_GDP-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       concluded that world GDP would change by plus or minus a few percent for a small increase in global mean temperature (up to around 2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C relative to the 1990 temperature level). Most studies assessed by Smith\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2001)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_estimate_of_climate_change_impacts_on_GDP_140-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Smith_estimate_of_climate_change_impacts_on_GDP-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       projected losses in world GDP for a medium increase in global mean temperature (above 2\xe2\x80\x933\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C relative to the 1990 temperature level), with increasing losses for greater temperature increases. This assessment is consistent with the findings of more recent studies, as reviewed by Hitz and Smith (2004).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_of_reasons_for_concern_141-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-update_of_reasons_for_concern-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Economic impacts are expected to vary regionally.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_of_reasons_for_concern_141-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-update_of_reasons_for_concern-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For a medium increase in global mean temperature (2\xe2\x80\x933\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C of warming, relative to the average temperature between 1990\xe2\x80\x932000), market sectors in low-latitude and less-developed areas might experience net costs due to climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-table_of_key_vulnerabilities_20-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-table_of_key_vulnerabilities-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On the other hand, market sectors in high-latitude and developed regions might experience net benefits for this level of warming. A global mean temperature increase above about 2\xe2\x80\x933\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (relative to 1990\xe2\x80\x932000) would very likely result in market sectors across all regions experiencing either declines in net benefits or rises in net costs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magnitudes_of_impact_49-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-magnitudes_of_impact-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Aggregate impacts have also been quantified in non-economic terms. For example, climate change over the 21st century is likely to adversely affect hundreds of millions of people through increased coastal flooding, reductions in water supplies, increased malnutrition and increased health impacts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar4_synthesis_reasons_for_concern_61-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ar4_synthesis_reasons_for_concern-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biological_systems">\n        Biological systems\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_ecosystems" title="Climate change and ecosystems">\n        Climate change and ecosystems\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Extinction_risk_from_global_warming" title="Extinction risk from global warming">\n        Extinction risk from global warming\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effect_of_climate_change_on_plant_biodiversity" title="Effect of climate change on plant biodiversity">\n        Effect of climate change on plant biodiversity\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_terrestrial_animals" title="Effects of climate change on terrestrial animals">\n        Effects of climate change on terrestrial animals\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_marine_mammals" title="Effects of climate change on marine mammals">\n        Effects of climate change on marine mammals\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Observed_impacts_on_biological_systems">\n        Observed impacts on biological systems\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_(low-res).png">\n         <img alt="refer to caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2267" data-file-width="1725" height="460" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_%28low-res%29.png/350px-A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_%28low-res%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_%28low-res%29.png/525px-A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_%28low-res%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_%28low-res%29.png/700px-A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_%28low-res%29.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_vast_array_of_physical_and_biological_systems_across_the_Earth_are_being_affected_by_human-induced_global_warming_(low-res).png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A vast array of physical and biological systems across the Earth are being affected by human-induced global warming.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_briefs_95-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-nasa_briefs-95">\n           [95]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       With very high confidence, Rosenzweig\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007) concluded that recent warming had strongly affected natural biological systems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hundreds of studies have documented responses of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">\n        ecosystems\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">\n        plants\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">\n        animals\n       </a>\n       to the climate changes that have already occurred.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">\n        <a href="#cite_note-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, in the Northern Hemisphere, species are almost uniformly moving their ranges northward and up in elevation in search of cooler temperatures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc_2008b_observed_ecosystem_impacts_144-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008b_observed_ecosystem_impacts-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Humans are very likely causing changes in regional temperatures to which plants and animals are responding.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc_2008b_observed_ecosystem_impacts_144-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008b_observed_ecosystem_impacts-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Projected_impacts_on_biological_systems">\n        Projected impacts on biological systems\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       By the year 2100, ecosystems will be exposed to atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       levels substantially higher than in the past 650,000 years, and global temperatures at least among the highest of those experienced in the past 740,000 years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fischlin_executive_summary_145-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fischlin_executive_summary-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Significant disruptions of ecosystems are projected to increase with future climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tar_synthesis_ecosystems_146-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tar_synthesis_ecosystems-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Examples of disruptions include disturbances such as fire, drought, pest\n       <a href="/wiki/Infestation" title="Infestation">\n        infestation\n       </a>\n       , invasion of species, storms, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">\n        coral bleaching\n       </a>\n       events. The stresses caused by climate change, added to other stresses on ecological systems (e.g., land conversion,\n       <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">\n        land degradation\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Harvest" title="Harvest">\n        harvesting\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">\n        pollution\n       </a>\n       ), threaten substantial damage to or complete loss of some unique ecosystems, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">\n        extinction\n       </a>\n       of some critically endangered species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tar_synthesis_ecosystems_146-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tar_synthesis_ecosystems-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n        <a href="#cite_note-147">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Climate change has been estimated to be a major driver of\n       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">\n        biodiversity loss\n       </a>\n       in cool\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conifer" title="Conifer">\n        conifer\n       </a>\n       forests,\n       <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">\n        savannas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">\n        mediterranean-climate\n       </a>\n       systems,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">\n        tropical forests\n       </a>\n       , in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_tundra" title="Arctic tundra">\n        Arctic tundra\n       </a>\n       , and in\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">\n        coral reefs\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_ecosystem_impacts_148-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-global_ecosystem_impacts-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In other ecosystems,\n       <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">\n        land-use\n       </a>\n       change may be a stronger driver of biodiversity loss at least in the near-term.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_ecosystem_impacts_148-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-global_ecosystem_impacts-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Beyond the year 2050, climate change may be the major driver for biodiversity loss globally.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_ecosystem_impacts_148-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-global_ecosystem_impacts-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A literature assessment by Fischlin\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fischlin_executive_summary_145-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fischlin_executive_summary-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       included a quantitative estimate of the number of species at increased risk of extinction due to climate change. With medium confidence, it was projected that approximately 20 to 30% of plant and animal species assessed so far (in an unbiased\n       <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(statistics)" title="Sampling (statistics)">\n        sample\n       </a>\n       ) would likely be at increasingly high risk of extinction should global mean temperatures exceed a warming of 2 to 3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C above pre-industrial temperature levels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fischlin_executive_summary_145-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fischlin_executive_summary-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The uncertainties in this estimate, however, are large: for a rise of about 2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C the percentage may be as low as 10%, or for about 3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C, as high as 40%, and depending on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biota_(ecology)" title="Biota (ecology)">\n        biota\n       </a>\n       (all living\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organisms\n       </a>\n       of an area, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">\n        flora\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">\n        fauna\n       </a>\n       considered as a unit)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">\n        <a href="#cite_note-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the range is between 1% and 80%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_ecosystem_impacts_148-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-global_ecosystem_impacts-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As global average temperature exceeds\n       <a href="/wiki/4_Degrees_and_Beyond_International_Climate_Conference" title="4 Degrees and Beyond International Climate Conference">\n        4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C\n       </a>\n       above pre-industrial levels, model projections suggested that there could be significant extinctions (40\xe2\x80\x9370% of species that were assessed) around the globe.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_ecosystem_impacts_148-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-global_ecosystem_impacts-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Assessing whether future changes in ecosystems will be beneficial or detrimental is largely based on how ecosystems are valued by human society.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For increases in global average temperature exceeding 1.5 to 2.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (relative to global temperatures over the years 1980\xe2\x80\x931999)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in concomitant atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       concentrations, projected changes in ecosystems will have predominantly negative consequences for biodiversity and ecosystems goods and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">\n        services\n       </a>\n       , e.g., water and food supply.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Abrupt_or_irreversible_changes">\n        Abrupt or irreversible changes\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Physical, ecological and social systems may respond in an abrupt,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-linear" title="Non-linear">\n        non-linear\n       </a>\n       or irregular way to climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singularities_153-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-singularities-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is as opposed to a smooth or regular response. A quantitative entity behaves "irregularly" when its\n       <a href="/wiki/System_dynamics" title="System dynamics">\n        dynamics\n       </a>\n       are\n       <a href="/wiki/Continuous_function" title="Continuous function">\n        discontinuous\n       </a>\n       (i.e., not smooth), nondifferentiable, unbounded, wildly varying, or otherwise ill-defined.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singularities_153-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-singularities-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Such behaviour is often termed "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mathematical_singularity" title="Mathematical singularity">\n        singular\n       </a>\n       ". Irregular behaviour in Earth systems may give rise to certain thresholds, which, when crossed, may lead to a large change in the system.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some singularities could potentially lead to severe impacts at regional or global scales.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-white_et_al_singularities_154-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-white_et_al_singularities-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Examples of "large-scale" singularities are discussed in the articles on\n       <a href="/wiki/Abrupt_climate_change" title="Abrupt climate change">\n        abrupt climate change\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_feedback" title="Climate change feedback">\n        climate change feedback\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Runaway_climate_change" title="Runaway climate change">\n        runaway climate change\n       </a>\n       . It is possible that human-induced climate change could trigger large-scale singularities, but the probabilities of triggering such events are, for the most part,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       poorly understood.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-white_et_al_singularities_154-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-white_et_al_singularities-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With low to medium confidence, Smith\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2001)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singularities_153-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-singularities-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       concluded that a rapid warming of more than 3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C above 1990 levels would exceed thresholds that would lead to large-scale discontinuities in the climate system.
