Since the assessment by Smith\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2001), improved scientific understanding provides more guidance for two large-scale singularities: the role of\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_cycle" title="Carbon cycle">\n        carbon cycle\n       </a>\n       feedbacks in future climate change (discussed below in the section on biogeochemical cycles) and the melting of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland_ice_sheet" title="Greenland ice sheet">\n        Greenland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Antarctic_ice_sheet" title="West Antarctic ice sheet">\n        West Antarctic ice sheets\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_of_reasons_for_concern_141-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-update_of_reasons_for_concern-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biogeochemical_cycles">\n        Biogeochemical cycles\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_feedback" title="Climate change feedback">\n        climate change feedback\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Climate change may have an effect on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_cycle" title="Carbon cycle">\n        carbon cycle\n       </a>\n       in an interactive "feedback" process. A feedback exists where an initial process triggers changes in a second process that in turn influences the initial process. A positive feedback intensifies the original process, and a negative feedback reduces it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR4_Synthesis_Report_120-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR4_Synthesis_Report-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :78\n       </sup>\n       Models suggest that the interaction of the climate system and the carbon cycle is one where the feedback effect is positive.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Assessing_key_vulnerabilities_and_the_risk_from_climate_change_156-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Assessing_key_vulnerabilities_and_the_risk_from_climate_change-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :792\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Using the A2 SRES emissions scenario, Schneider\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Assessing_key_vulnerabilities_and_the_risk_from_climate_change_156-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Assessing_key_vulnerabilities_and_the_risk_from_climate_change-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :789\n       </sup>\n       found that this effect led to additional warming by the years 2090\xe2\x80\x932100 (relative to the 1990\xe2\x80\x932000) of 0.1\xe2\x80\x931.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C. This estimate was made with high confidence. The climate projections made in the IPCC Fourth Assessment Report summarized earlier of 1.1\xe2\x80\x936.4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C account for this feedback effect. On the other hand, with medium confidence, Schneider\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (2007)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Assessing_key_vulnerabilities_and_the_risk_from_climate_change_156-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Assessing_key_vulnerabilities_and_the_risk_from_climate_change-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :789\n       </sup>\n       commented that additional releases of GHGs were possible from permafrost, peat lands, wetlands, and large stores of marine hydrates at high latitudes.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Greenland_and_West_Antarctic_Ice_sheets">\n        Greenland and West Antarctic Ice sheets\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       With medium confidence, authors of AR4\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magnitudes_of_impact_49-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-magnitudes_of_impact-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       concluded that with a global average temperature increase of 1\xe2\x80\x934\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (relative to temperatures over the years 1990\xe2\x80\x932000), at least a partial deglaciation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland_ice_sheet" title="Greenland ice sheet">\n        Greenland ice sheet\n       </a>\n       , and possibly the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Antarctic_ice_sheet" title="West Antarctic ice sheet">\n        West Antarctic ice sheets\n       </a>\n       would occur. The estimated timescale for partial deglaciation was centuries to millennia, and would contribute 4 to 6 metres (13 to 20\xc2\xa0ft) or more to sea level rise over this period.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Atlantic_Meridional_Overturning_Circulation">\n        Atlantic Meridional Overturning Circulation\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Shutdown_of_thermohaline_circulation" title="Shutdown of thermohaline circulation">\n        Shutdown of thermohaline circulation\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png">\n         <img alt="refer to caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="1100" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png/320px-Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png/480px-Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png/640px-Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png 2x" width="320"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thermohaline_Circulation_2.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         This map shows the general location and direction of the warm surface (red) and cold deep water (blue) currents of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Thermohaline_circulation" title="Thermohaline circulation">\n          thermohaline circulation\n         </a>\n         .\n         <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">\n          Salinity\n         </a>\n         is represented by color in units of the Practical Salinity Scale. Low values (blue) are less saline, while high values (orange) are more saline.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n          <a href="#cite_note-157">\n           [157]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Atlantic Meridional Overturning Circulation (AMOC) is an important component of the Earth\'s climate system, characterized by a northward flow of warm, salty water in the upper layers of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_ocean" title="Atlantic ocean">\n        Atlantic\n       </a>\n       and a southward flow of colder water in the deep Atlantic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change_158-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :5\n       </sup>\n       The AMOC is equivalently known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermohaline_circulation" title="Thermohaline circulation">\n        thermohaline circulation\n       </a>\n       (THC).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_of_reasons_for_concern_141-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-update_of_reasons_for_concern-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Potential impacts associated with MOC changes include reduced warming or (in the case of abrupt change) absolute cooling of northern high-latitude areas near\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">\n        Greenland\n       </a>\n       and north-western Europe, an increased warming of\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">\n        Southern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       high-latitudes, tropical drying, as well as changes to\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_ecosystem" title="Marine ecosystem">\n        marine ecosystems\n       </a>\n       , terrestrial vegetation, oceanic\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       uptake, oceanic oxygen concentrations, and shifts in fisheries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to an assessment by the US\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_Change_Science_Program" title="Climate Change Science Program">\n        Climate Change Science Program\n       </a>\n       (CCSP, 2008b),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change_158-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :5\n       </sup>\n       it is very likely (greater than 90% probability, based on expert judgement)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change_158-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :12\n       </sup>\n       that the strength of the AMOC will decrease over the course of the 21st century. Warming is still expected to occur over most of the European region downstream of the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Current" title="North Atlantic Current">\n        North Atlantic Current\n       </a>\n       in response to increasing GHGs, as well as over\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       . Although it is very unlikely (less than 10% probability, based on expert judgement)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change_158-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :12\n       </sup>\n       that the AMOC will collapse in the 21st century, the potential consequences of such a collapse could be severe.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change_158-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ccsp_abrupt_climate_change-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :5\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Irreversibilities">\n        Irreversibilities\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commitment_to_radiative_forcing">\n        Commitment to radiative forcing\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Emissions of GHGs are a potentially irreversible commitment to sustained\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiative_forcing" title="Radiative forcing">\n        radiative forcing\n       </a>\n       in the future.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albritton_irreversible_radiative_forcing_160-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-albritton_irreversible_radiative_forcing-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The contribution of a GHG to radiative forcing depends on the gas\'s ability to trap\n       <a href="/wiki/Infrared" title="Infrared">\n        infrared\n       </a>\n       (heat) radiation, the concentration of the gas in the atmosphere, and the length of time the gas resides in the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albritton_irreversible_radiative_forcing_160-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-albritton_irreversible_radiative_forcing-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       is the most important anthropogenic GHG.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_2007_causes_of_climate_change_161-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_2007_causes_of_climate_change-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While more than half of the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       emitted is currently removed from the atmosphere within a century, some fraction (about 20%) of emitted\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       remains in the atmosphere for many thousands of years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">\n        <a href="#cite_note-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Consequently,\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       emitted today is potentially an irreversible commitment to sustained radiative forcing over thousands of years.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This commitment may not be truly irreversible should techniques be developed to remove\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       or other GHGs directly from the atmosphere, or to block sunlight to induce cooling.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_irreversible_climate_change_32-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-solomon_irreversible_climate_change-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Techniques of this sort are referred to as\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_engineering" title="Climate engineering">\n        geoengineering\n       </a>\n       . Little is known about the effectiveness, costs or potential\n       <a href="/wiki/Unintended_consequences" title="Unintended consequences">\n        side-effects\n       </a>\n       of geoengineering options.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barker_geoengineering_163-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-barker_geoengineering-163">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some geoengineering options, such as blocking sunlight, would not prevent further\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">\n        ocean acidification\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barker_geoengineering_163-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-barker_geoengineering-163">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Irreversible_impacts">\n        Irreversible impacts\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Human-induced climate change may lead to irreversible impacts on physical, biological, and social systems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">\n        <a href="#cite_note-164">\n         [164]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are a number of examples of climate change impacts that may be irreversible, at least over the timescale of many human generations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_irreversibilities_165-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_irreversibilities-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These include the large-scale singularities described above \xe2\x80\x93 changes in carbon cycle feedbacks, the melting of the Greenland and West Antarctic ice sheets, and changes to the AMOC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_irreversibilities_165-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_irreversibilities-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In biological systems, the extinction of species would be an irreversible impact.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_irreversibilities_165-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_irreversibilities-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In social systems, unique\n       <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">\n        cultures\n       </a>\n       may be lost due to climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schneider_irreversibilities_165-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schneider_irreversibilities-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, humans living on\n       <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">\n        atoll\n       </a>\n       islands face risks due to sea-level rise, sea-surface warming, and increased frequency and intensity of extreme weather events.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">\n        <a href="#cite_note-166">\n         [166]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Benefits_of_global_warming">\n        Benefits of global warming\n        <span id="Benefits_of_Global_Warming">\n        </span>\n        <span id="Benefits">\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In some locations and industries global warming may increase productivity, though the IPCC cautions that "Estimates agree on the size of the impact (small relative to economic growth), and 17 of the 20 impact estimates shown in Figure 10-1 are negative. Losses accelerate with greater warming, and estimates diverge."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">\n        <a href="#cite_note-167">\n         [167]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The identified benefits are listed below.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="CO2_fertilisation_effect">\n        CO2 fertilisation effect\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        CO2\n       </a>\n       is one of the substances which plants require to grow. Increasing its amount in the air contributes to:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Improved agriculture in some high latitude regions\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">\n         <a href="#cite_note-168">\n          [168]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Increased growing season in\n        <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">\n         Greenland\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">\n         <a href="#cite_note-169">\n          [169]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Increased productivity of\n        <a href="/wiki/Bitter_orange" title="Bitter orange">\n         sour orange\n        </a>\n        trees\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">\n         <a href="#cite_note-170">\n          [170]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Increased vegetation activity in high northern latitudes\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">\n         <a href="#cite_note-171">\n          [171]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Increased plankton biomass in the North Pacific Subtropical Gyre\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">\n         <a href="#cite_note-172">\n          [172]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Recent increase in forest growth\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">\n         <a href="#cite_note-173">\n          [173]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Increased Arctic tundra plant reproduction\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">\n         <a href="#cite_note-174">\n          [174]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_health">\n        Human health\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Winter deaths might decline as temperatures warm. However, this is disputed for at least some regions. For example,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">\n         <a href="#cite_note-175">\n          [175]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        states "Although excess winter deaths evidently do exist, winter cold severity no longer predicts the numbers affected. We conclude that no evidence exists that excess winter deaths in England and Wales will fall if winters warm with climate change."\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ice-free_Northwest_Passage">\n        Ice-free Northwest Passage\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Ships will travel on a shorter route between the Pacific and Atlantic oceans\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">\n         <a href="#cite_note-176">\n          [176]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_population_changes">\n        Animal population changes\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Some animals will benefit from the warming:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Increase in\n        <a href="/wiki/Chinstrap_penguin" title="Chinstrap penguin">\n         chinstrap\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Gentoo_penguin" title="Gentoo penguin">\n         gentoo penguins\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">\n         <a href="#cite_note-177">\n          [177]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Bigger\n        <a href="/wiki/Marmot" title="Marmot">\n         marmots\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">\n         <a href="#cite_note-178">\n          [178]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_opinion">\n        Scientific opinion\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">\n        Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change\n       </a>\n       (IPCC) has published several major assessments on the effects of global warming.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">\n        <a href="#cite_note-179">\n         [179]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its most recent comprehensive impact assessment was published in 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">\n        <a href="#cite_note-180">\n         [180]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Publications describing the effects of climate change have also been produced by the following organizations:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">\n         American Association for the Advancement of Science\n        </a>\n        (AAAS)\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">\n         <a href="#cite_note-181">\n          [181]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A report by the\n        <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Environmental_Assessment_Agency" title="Netherlands Environmental Assessment Agency">\n         Netherlands Environmental Assessment Agency\n        </a>\n        , the\n        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Meteorological_Institute" title="Royal Netherlands Meteorological Institute">\n         Royal Netherlands Meteorological Institute\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Wageningen_University_and_Research_Centre" title="Wageningen University and Research Centre">\n         Wageningen University and Research Centre\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">\n         <a href="#cite_note-182">\n          [182]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        UK AVOID research programme\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">\n         <a href="#cite_note-183">\n          [183]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A report by the UK\n        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">\n         Royal Society\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="US National Academy of Sciences">\n         US National Academy of Sciences\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">\n         <a href="#cite_note-184">\n          [184]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_South_Wales" title="University of New South Wales">\n         University of New South Wales\n        </a>\n        Climate Change Research Centre\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">\n         <a href="#cite_note-185">\n          [185]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_National_Research_Council" title="US National Research Council">\n         US National Research Council\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">\n         <a href="#cite_note-186">\n          [186]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">\n         <a href="#cite_note-187">\n          [187]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       A report by Molina\n       <i>\n        et al.\n       </i>\n       (no date)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">\n        <a href="#cite_note-188">\n         [188]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       states:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote>\n       <p>\n        The overwhelming evidence of human-caused climate change documents both current impacts with significant costs and extraordinary future risks to society and natural systems\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_data_and_tools">\n        NASA data and tools\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       NASA has released public data and tools to predict how temperature and rainfall patterns worldwide may change through to the year 2100 caused by increasing carbon dioxide in Earth\xe2\x80\x99s atmosphere. The dataset shows projected changes worldwide on a regional level simulated by 21 climate models. The data can be viewed on a daily timescale for individual cities and towns and may be used to conduct climate risk assessments to predict the local and global effects of weather dangers, for example droughts, floods, heat waves and declines in agriculture productivity, and help plan responses to global warming effects.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">\n        <a href="#cite_note-189">\n         [189]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">\n        Footnotes\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       <sup>\n        1\n       </sup>\n       The TAR\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uncertainty_in_the_TAR_190-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Uncertainty_in_the_TAR-190">\n         [190]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and AR4\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       that are referred to in this article use specific and quantitative language to describe uncertainty. This language is intended to provide an indication of the level of confidence that IPCC authors have about a particular finding. The qualitative language used to describe uncertainty has a quantitative scale associated with it. The quantitative values for qualitative terms are intended to ensure that confidence levels are interpreted correctly. The is because qualitative statements, e.g., using the word "likely", can be interpreted differently in quantitative terms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">\n        <a href="#cite_note-191">\n         [191]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :44\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Confidence levels used in the TAR:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">\n        <a href="#cite_note-192">\n         [192]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Very High = 95% or greater\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        High = 67\xe2\x80\x9395%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Medium = 33\xe2\x80\x9367%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Low = 5\xe2\x80\x9333%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Very Low = 5% or less\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Confidence statements made in AR4 are listed below:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Very high confidence: At least 9 out of 10 chance of being correct\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        High confidence: About 8 out of 10 chance " " "\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Medium confidence: About 5 out of 10 chance " " "\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Low confidence: About 2 out of 10 chance " " "\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Very low confidence: Less than a 1 out of 10 chance " " "\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       IPCC (2012)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">\n        <a href="#cite_note-193">\n         [193]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       uses the following terms: "very low", "low", "medium", "high", and "very high confidence". Unlike the TAR and AR4, the scale is qualitative rather than quantitative.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The quantitative values used by IPCC authors are "subjective" probabilities,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uncertainty_in_the_TAR_190-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Uncertainty_in_the_TAR-190">\n         [190]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">\n        <a href="#cite_note-194">\n         [194]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       also known as "personalist" or "\n       <a href="/wiki/Bayesian_probability" title="Bayesian probability">\n        Bayesian\n       </a>\n       " probabilities,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_CCSP_report_on_uncertainty_195-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-US_CCSP_report_on_uncertainty-195">\n         [195]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and reflect the expert judgement of IPCC authors. In this formulation, probability is not only a function of an event, but also the state of information that is available to the person making the assessment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_CCSP_report_on_uncertainty_195-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-US_CCSP_report_on_uncertainty-195">\n         [195]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In this framework, assigned probabilities may change as more or different information becomes available.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_CCSP_report_on_uncertainty_195-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-US_CCSP_report_on_uncertainty-195">\n         [195]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The IPCC also uses another scale to describe the likelihood of a particular event occurring.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is different from the confidence scales described above, and it is possible to assign confidence values to statements of likelihood. For example, the judgement that an event is improbable (e.g., rolling a\n       <a href="/wiki/Dice" title="Dice">\n        dice\n       </a>\n       twice and getting a six both times) may be assigned a high level of scientific confidence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also, the probability that an event has an even chance of occurring (e.g., a tossed\n       <a href="/wiki/Coin" title="Coin">\n        coin\n       </a>\n       coming up heads) may also be assigned a high level of confidence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">\n        Notes\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <ol class="references">\n        <li id="cite_note-1">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          <b>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-1">\n            ^\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite
